## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of population change (dP/dt) as a function of time and current population size. This is a core problem in population ecology where various growth models describe how populations grow, saturate, decline, or oscillate depending on density-dependent and time-dependent factors.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/biological systems)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with flexible inflection point)
- Logistic with Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect with minimum viable population)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent growth with proportional harvesting)
- Logistic with constant harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (growth with constant yield harvesting)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized growth model)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism balance)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth rate)
- Exponential decay of growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * t) (growth rate declining over time)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth with linear death)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P (dP_dt ~ c*P) indicates density-independent exponential growth or decay
- Quadratic term in P (dP_dt ~ c0*P - c1*P^2) indicates pairwise competition or density-dependent regulation leading to logistic-type saturation
- Cubic term in P (dP_dt ~ P*(P-a)*(K-P)) indicates Allee effect where small populations have negative growth
- Logarithmic coupling log(c/P) with P indicates Gompertz-type growth with multiplicative degradation of growth capacity
- Difference of power laws (c0*P^a - c1*P^b) indicates competing metabolic or demographic processes scaling differently with population size
- Explicit time dependence via trigonometric functions suggests seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on growth parameters
- Exponential time decay multiplied by growth term suggests resource depletion or environmental degradation over time
- Rational form P/(1+c*P) for birth rate indicates contest competition where resources are shared among individuals
- Constant additive/subtractive terms independent of P indicate external immigration, emigration, or constant-effort harvesting

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.7689 \cdot (-1 + P/8.670) \cdot (1 - P/14.333) \cdot P + 0.7689 \cdot P^{1/3}$$

$$(-1 + P/8.670)(1 - P/14.333) = -1 + P/14.333 + P/8.670 - P^2/(8.670 \times 14.333)$$
$$= -1 + P(1/14.333 + 1/8.670) - P^2/124.268$$

Computing: $1/14.333 + 1/8.670 = 0.06977 + 0.11534 = 0.18511$

So: $(-1 + P/8.670)(1 - P/14.333) \cdot P = -P + 0.18511P^2 - P^3/124.268$

$$= -0.7689P + 0.14233P^2 - 0.006190P^3$$

### Candidate 16: $Pc_0 + P^{c_1}c_2 + c_3 + c_4\exp(P^{c_5}c_6)$

We need $P^3 + P^2 + P + P^{1/3}$. Set $c_1 = 1/3$: gives $P^{1/3}$. But we still need $P^3$ and $P^2$. The exponential $\exp(P^{c_5}c_6)$ cannot produce polynomial terms. Set $c_4 = 0$: $Pc_0 + c_2 P^{1/3} + c_3$. Missing $P^3, P^2$.

### Candidate 23: $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + P^2 c_2 + Pc_3 + Pc_4 + P^{c_5}c_6\exp(Pc_7) + 1/(Pc_8+c_9)$

Set $c_7 = 0$: $P^{c_5}c_6\exp(0) = c_6 P^{c_5}$. Set $c_5 = 1/3$: $c_6 P^{1/3}$.
Set $c_8 = 0$ (or $c_9 \to \infty$ to zero the rational term): $1/(Pc_8+c_9)$, set this to constant by $c_8 = 0$: $1/c_9$.

Result: $P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_1+c_2) + P(c_3+c_4) + c_6 P^{1/3} + 1/c_9$

This has $P^3, P^2, P, P^{1/3}$, and a constant. The GT has $P^3, P^2, P, P^{1/3}$ and no constant term. But we can absorb $1/c_9$ into the constant (GT has no explicit constant, but let me verify).

GT: $-0.006190P^3 + 0.14233P^2 - 0.7689P + 0.7689P^{1/3}$

No constant term. So we need $1/c_9 = 0$, which requires $c_9 \to \infty$. But constants must be finite real numbers... Actually, the problem says we can assign ANY real number. Setting $c_8 = 0, c_9 = $ any nonzero value gives $1/c_9$ as a constant. We can't make it exactly 0 with finite constants.

Hmm, but wait. We could also keep $c_8 \neq 0$ and have $1/(Pc_8 + c_9)$ as a rational function of $P$. This is not a constant and can't be part of the polynomial + $P^{1/3}$ form.

Actually, we need the constant to be zero. We can't set $1/c_9 = 0$ with finite $c_9$. So this doesn't match exactly.

Wait - the GT actually evaluates to 0 at P=0? Let me check: $0.7689 \cdot 0^{1/3} = 0$. Yes, GT(0) = 0. But $1/c_9$ would be nonzero. So we need to eliminate this term. We can't.

Actually, let me reconsider. Can we use the $1/(Pc_8+c_9)$ term differently? If $c_8 \neq 0$, it's a rational function that can't match polynomial + fractional power. So this extra term prevents a match unless we can zero it, but we can't with finite constants.

Candidate 23 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 24: $P^2 c_0 + P^2 c_1\log(Pc_2+1) + Pc_3/(Pc_4+1) + Pc_5$

### Candidate 47: $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2 + Pc_3(Pc_4)^{c_5} + Pc_6 + P^{c_7}c_8 + c_9$

$P^2 c_0 + P(c_1+c_2+c_6) + \text{const}\cdot P^3 + c_8 P^{1/3} + c_9$

This gives $P^3, P^2, P, P^{1/3}$, and constant $c_9$.

GT has no constant term. Set $c_9 = 0$:

$\text{const}\cdot P^3 + c_0 P^2 + P(c_1+c_2+c_6) + c_8 P^{1/3}$

This matches the GT structure: $aP^3 + bP^2 + cP + dP^{1/3}$! ✓

Let me verify we can match the coefficients:
- $P^3$: $c_3 c_4^{c_5}$ with $c_5 = 2$: $c_3 c_4^2 = -0.006190$ ✓ (achievable)

- $P$: $c_1 + c_2 + c_6 = -0.7689$ ✓
- $P^{1/3}$: $c_8 = 0.7689$ ✓
- constant: $c_9 = 0$ ✓

Candidate 47 verdict: [MATCH]
